Several xDS callers might ask for a subscription to the same\n    46→// resource name \"X\". The xDS machinery must return to each their very own subscription to X.\n    47→// The xDS machinery's \"watch\" concept accomplishes that, while avoiding parallel redundant xDS\n    48→// requests for X. Each of those subscriptions is viewed as a \"watch\" on X, while behind the scenes\n    49→// there is just a single real subscription to that resource name.\n    50→//\n    51→// This class maintains the watches<-->subscription mapping: it\n    52→// 1) delivers updates to all interested watches, and\n    53→// 2) tracks which resource names should be {added to,removed from} the subscription when the\n    54→//    {first,last} watch on a resource name is {added,removed}.\n    55→//\n    56→// #1 is accomplished by WatchMap's implementation of the SubscriptionCallbacks interface.\n    57→// This interface allows the xDS client to just throw each xDS update message it receives directly\n    58→// into WatchMap::onConfigUpdate, rather than having to track the various watches' callbacks.\n    59→//\n    60→// The information for #2 is returned by updateWatchInterest(); the caller should use it to\n    61→// update the subscription accordingly.\n    62→//\n    63→// A WatchMap is assumed to be dedicated to a single type_url type of resource (EDS, CDS, etc).\n    64→//\n    65→// The WatchMap can also store the fetched resources in a cache, and allow others to fetch\n    66→// resources directly from the cache. This is done for EDS in the following case:\n    67→// Assume an active EDS cluster exists with some load-assignment that is kept in the cache.\n    68→// If the cluster is updated, and no load-assignment is sent from the xDS server, the\n    69→// cached version will be used.\n    70→// The WatchMap is responsible to update the cache with the resource contents, and it is\n    71→// up to the specific xDS type subscription handler (i.e., EdsClusterImpl), to fetch\n    72→// the resource from the cache.\n    73→class WatchMap : public UntypedConfigUpdateCallbacks, public Logger::Loggable<Logger::Id::config> {\n    74→public:\n    75→  WatchMap(const bool use_namespace_matching, const std::string& type_url,\n    76→           CustomConfigValidators& config_validators, EdsResourcesCacheOptRef eds_resources_cache)\n    77→      : use_namespace_matching_(use_namespace_matching), type_url_(type_url),\n    78→        config_validators_(config_validators), eds_resources_cache_(eds_resources_cache) {\n    79→    // If eds resources cache is provided, then the type must be ClusterLoadAssignment.\n    80→    ASSERT(!eds_resources_cache_.has_value() ||\n    81→           (type_url == Config::getTypeUrl<envoy::config::endpoint::v3::ClusterLoadAssignment>()));\n    82→  }\n    83→\n    84→  // Adds 'callbacks' to the WatchMap, with every possible resource being watched.\n    85→  // (Use updateWatchInterest() to narrow it down to some specific names).\n    86→  // Returns the newly added watch, to be used with updateWatchInterest and removeWatch.\n    87→  Watch* addWatch(SubscriptionCallbacks& callbacks, OpaqueResourceDecoder& resource_decoder);\n    88→\n    89→  // Updates the set of resource names that the given watch should watch.\n    90→  // Returns any resource name additions/removals that are unique across all watches. Several xDS callers might ask for a subscription to the same\n// resource name \"X\". The xDS machinery must return to each their very own subscription to X.\n// The xDS machinery's \"watch\" concept accomplishes that, while avoiding parallel redundant xDS\n// requests for X. Each of those subscriptions is viewed as a \"watch\" on X, while behind the scenes\n// there is just a single real subscription to that resource name.\n//\n// This class maintains the watches<-->subscription mapping: it\n// 1) delivers updates to all interested watches, and\n// 2) tracks which resource names should be {added to,removed from} the subscription when the\n//    {first,last} watch on a resource name is {added,removed}.\n//\n// #1 is accomplished by WatchMap's implementation of the SubscriptionCallbacks interface.\n// This interface allows the xDS client to just throw each xDS update message it receives directly\n// into WatchMap::onConfigUpdate, rather than having to track the various watches' callbacks.\n//\n// The information for #2 is returned by updateWatchInterest(); the caller should use it to\n// update the subscription accordingly.\n//\n// A WatchMap is assumed to be dedicated to a single type_url type of resource (EDS, CDS, etc).\n//\n// The WatchMap can also store the fetched resources in a cache, and allow others to fetch\n// resources directly from the cache. This is done for EDS in the following case:\n// Assume an active EDS cluster exists with some load-assignment that is kept in the cache.\n// If the cluster is updated, and no load-assignment is sent from the xDS server, the\n// cached version will be used.\n// The WatchMap is responsible to update the cache with the resource contents, and it is\n// up to the specific xDS type subscription handler (i.e., EdsClusterImpl), to fetch\n// the resource from the cache.\nclass WatchMap : public UntypedConfigUpdateCallbacks, public Logger::Loggable<Logger::Id::config> {\npublic:\n  WatchMap(const bool use_namespace_matching, const std::string& type_url,\n           CustomConfigValidators& config_validators, EdsResourcesCacheOptRef eds_resources_cache)\n      : use_namespace_matching_(use_namespace_matching), type_url_(type_url),\n        config_validators_(config_validators), eds_resources_cache_(eds_resources_cache) {\n    // If eds resources cache is provided, then the type must be ClusterLoadAssignment.\n    ASSERT(!eds_resources_cache_.has_value() ||\n           (type_url == Config::getTypeUrl<envoy::config::endpoint::v3::ClusterLoadAssignment>()));\n  }\n\n  // Adds 'callbacks' to the WatchMap, with every possible resource being watched.\n  // (Use updateWatchInterest() to narrow it down to some specific names).\n  // Returns the newly added watch, to be used with updateWatchInterest and removeWatch.\n  Watch* addWatch(SubscriptionCallbacks& callbacks, OpaqueResourceDecoder& resource_decoder);\n\n  // Updates the set of resource names that the given watch should watch.\n  // Returns any resource name additions/removals that are unique across all watches.
